<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_346eb37d-79ab-4bf7-b391-7d63e60ffc14'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer5212125355158161257">Harper Price, peerless Southern belle, was born ready for a Homecoming tiara.   <span id="freeText5212125355158161257" style="display:none">Harper Price, peerless Southern belle, was born ready for a Homecoming tiara. But after a strange run-in at the dance imbues her with incredible abilities, Harper's destiny takes a turn for the seriously weird. She becomes a Paladin, one of an ancient line of guardians with agility, super strength and lethal fighting instincts.<br /><br />Just when life can't get any more disastrously crazy, Harper finds out who she's charged to protect: David Stark, school reporter, subject of a mysterious prophecy and possibly Harper's least favorite person. But things get complicated when Harper starts falling for him—and discovers that David's own fate could very well be to destroy Earth.<br /><br />With snappy banter, cotillion dresses, non-stop action and a touch of magic, this new young adult series from bestseller Rachel Hawkins is going to make y'all beg for more.</span>

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/21166726-kat-e-larson"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1370822518i/21166726._UY100_CR4,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/21166726-kat-e-larson">Kat!e Larson</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It's similar in a "teenage girl gets paranormal powers and has to save the world while still trying to be a normal teenager" sort of way. And, contrar<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It's similar in a "teenage girl gets paranormal powers and has to save the world while still trying to be a normal teenager" sort of way. And, contrary to what the previous responder said, there ARE witches (though they prefer "Mage.") But it's pretty different. It's very character-based, and Harper isn't anything like Buffy.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_879197963" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/879197963" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/879197963?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=high-school">high-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=awesome-guy">awesome-guy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=kick-ass-heroine">kick-ass-heroine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer879197963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9346958248400607246"><blockquote>
  <i>Once again, my chest tightened, and there was that weird fluttering sensation that was like butterflies. But it couldn’t be butterflies. I did not have butterflies over David Stark.</i>
</blockquote>25% of the way in, I was sure I would give this book a 4, but I ended up wanting to fling this book at Harper's head. This book may be really, really cute, <b>but overall, it's just an overextended love triangle without much of a plot.</b> Nothing of importance happens in this book.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397017072ra/9219399.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This was not a bad book by any means. I</span>
  <span id="freeText9346958248400607246" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Once again, my chest tightened, and there was that weird fluttering sensation that was like butterflies. But it couldn’t be butterflies. I did not have butterflies over David Stark.</i>
</blockquote>25% of the way in, I was sure I would give this book a 4, but I ended up wanting to fling this book at Harper's head. This book may be really, really cute, <b>but overall, it's just an overextended love triangle without much of a plot.</b> Nothing of importance happens in this book.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397017072ra/9219399.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was not a bad book by any means. I absolutely adored the main character, the relationships and the friendships were wonderfully written, the high school kids were just plain cute. But seriously, <b>there was no fucking point to the love triangle</b>, and I wanted to bash my head in every time the WONDERFUL BESTEST BOYFRIEND EVER <b>Ryan</b> clashed with BROODING HIPSTER ASSHOLE (with a heart of gold) <b>David</b>. <br><br>Not since <b>
  <i>Unearthly</i>
</b> has a love triangle been so <b>dragged out to agonizing nonresolution</b> until the very fucking end. There was no fucking point to this love triangle. Why did it need a love triangle? Why could she not protect one guy and be his friend while remaining with her current boyfriend?! Why?!<br><br>If you don't mind the love triangle, I would recommend this book, because it was seriously sweet, as in the "I just ate a half pound of French chocolate truffles, but who cares, bitches, they're TRUFFLES!" sort of sweet. It was the good kind of sweetness. This book is so lighthearted and cute. But <i>that love triangle</i>, man!<br><br><u>The Summary</u>: <blockquote>
  <i>“So, Harper Jane Price. Are you ready to accept your destiny?”</i>
</blockquote>It's silly, but if Harper hadn't forgotten her lip gloss, this never would have happened.<br><br>Harper Jane Price, Southern Belle extraordinaire, is perfect. She has a great life (let's not talk about her dead sister), a loving, wonderful boyfriend <b>Ryan</b>, fantastic friends, adoring parents, and a bright future.<br><br>Southern Belles are beautiful on the surface, sure, but what you might fail to notice upon first glance is that they have a backbone made of steel. Harper is one of those "I don't know how she does it" type of gal. Great grades, school president, popular, admired. Until the night it all starts to unravel. Until the night she forgot her lipgloss at the homecoming dance. Because then she had to borrow her friend's lip gloss. Because she stepped into the bathroom, only to encounter her school janitor, Mr. Hall, bloody and battered.<blockquote>
  <i>His breath was coming out in short gasps, and there was a dark red stain spreading across his expansive belly. There was no doubt in my mind that he was dying.</i>
</blockquote>Before dying, Mr. Hall breathes an ice-cold breath of air into Harper's lungs (ew), and whispers to her...<blockquote>
  <i>“Look after him, okay?” he said, his eyes looking glazed again. “Make sure he’s...he’s safe.”</i>
</blockquote>WTF?! So there's Harper, in her Homecoming outfit (which cost over $1k), hovering over a dead man. SHIT. And to make it worse, at that moment, her history teacher barges in. Not only does he insult her...<blockquote>
  <i>“I really can’t think of a worse choice,” he said, still smiling, “than the bimbo who wrote a paper on the history of shoes for my class.”</i>
</blockquote>But he tries to kill her!! He doesn't exactly succeed, because somehow Harper finds the strength in herself to kick his ass. <blockquote>
  <i>The sword was still poised in the air when I came to an abrupt stop and sunk the heel into his throat, right under his jaw.</i>
</blockquote>He really shouldn't have called her a bimbo.<br><br>So crap, what the fuck is all this?! Before he died, Mr. Hall muttered something about a "Pal," and some vague shit about protection. After Googling this shit, Harper theorizes that the "Pal" means Paladin (Thank you, World of Warcraft, really!). So the only thing Harper has to figure out now is <i>who</i> she's meant to protect.<blockquote>
  <i>Mr. Hall hadn’t been a superhero. He’d been a Paladin, and that was . . . different, right? And what—or who—had been his noble cause?<br>What was mine?</i>
</blockquote>She'll figure it out eventually. Meanwhile, there's school to deal with. Not to mention asshole hipster extraordinaire <b>David Stark</b>. Everyone has a thorn in their life, and David Stark is Harper's pain in the ass. He's the only skinny-jean wearing hipster in the entire school, and <b>ever since childhood, David's mission has been to take Harper down.</b> Currently, he's on the school paper, writing vicious articles about her, and this latest one is the last fucking straw.<blockquote>
  <i>Under the picture of me and Bee, there was a smaller caption: Homecoming Queen misses crowning under mysterious circumstances. My eyes darted over the rest of the article as my heart started pounding. “...hiding in the boys’ room...violently ill...tension between the ‘Queen Bee’ and her underling, Bee Franklin...this reporter...”</i>
</blockquote>Harper Price is PISSED, and she's going to murder that asshole. Except she can't.<blockquote>
  <i>Whatever the reason, my right hand shot up to slap David Stark across the face. <br>Half an inch from David’s cheek, my hand stopped in midair. And it wasn’t because I had some crisis of conscience, either. It was like my hand hit an invisible wall right by his head.</i>
</blockquote>Well, fuck. <b>It turns out that Harper is a Paladin chosen to protect David.</b> And as much as she hates him, she can't hurt him. In fact, she has to protect him with her life. What will become of Harper's life? Her relationship with her friends, her wonderful boyfriend? Is she prepared to give it all up to protect David?<blockquote>
  <i>I withdrew my hand. <b>“No, thank you.”</b><br>Saylor and David both stared.<br>“I appreciate your offer very much,” I continued. “But I’m afraid I have to refuse.”</i>
</blockquote><b>Well, we all know that it's not that simple</b>. But Harper already has so much on her plate. How is she going to deal with David...while trying to maintain her relationship with Ryan?!<blockquote>
  <i>“But you’re always arguing with him. Or talking about him. Or competing with him. And sometimes I wonder how you can be so obsessed with someone you supposedly hate.”</i>
</blockquote>And Ryan is so understanding. He's trying to understand WHY she's spending so much time away from him. Harper is so busy sneaking around with David <b>talking about being a Paladin</b> that she just doesn't have any time for the perfect Ryan anymore. And Ryan really is perfect.<blockquote>
  <i>“I love you,” he said at last. “You know that. But it’s...it’s like we’re speaking two different languages most of the time. Harper.” He tugged on my hand. “If there’s something going on with you, you can tell me, okay?”</i>
</blockquote>Even as he suspects something's going on between David and his girlfriend...<blockquote>
  <i>“You guys seemed pretty...intense yesterday,” Ryan said, dropping my hand.<br>“Yeah, we were intensely arguing over him writing that stupid article,” I said even as I had a sudden vision of me and David, laughing in his car. Hugging. God, we had hugged.</i>
</blockquote>THAT'S THE ENTIRE FUCKING BOOK.<br><br><u>The Premise</u>: The Paladin thing is just...strange. This is pretty original, in that I've rarely seen the concept of <b>the Paladin</b> used, and to be honest...it doesn't quite work. It's just a protector, nothing more. Someone assigned to protect a person, and the concept was not convincing. The mythology behind it wasn't well-drawn enough to be truly attractive, and overall, I just found the concept rather baffling. This book completely lacks <i>Hex Hall</i>'s magic in that sense. <b>It is an urban fantasy that's too light on the fantasy, with almost no relevant action at all.</b><br><br><u>Harper</u>: She is just a fabulous narrator.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397017072ra/9219400.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The quintessential Steel Magnolia. She reminds me a little bit of <b>Mac in the <i>Fever</i></b> series. Before you go running away, I have to make a case for Harper. She is young, she is 17, and she is so utterly competent. <b>Think of Harper as Mac 4.0</b>. Harper has none of Mac's immaturity, on the contrary, Harper is <b>astoundingly capable.</b> She is cheerleader, class president, Homecoming organizer, she's in the Future Business Leaders of America, she's got great grades, she's got a gentle nature, she holds it all together. Most of it had to do with the fact that she's trying to get over her sister's death. Harper organizes away her grief with perfection. So much that her parents worry about her.<blockquote>
  <i>And the next time I did school stuff in the middle of the night, I just did it in my closet with the door locked. Honestly, what is wrong with this country when striving for excellence means you need antidepressants?</i>
</blockquote>I absolutely loved Harper. She is never judgmental, she is a Southern Belle with none of the annoying characteristics, and honestly, I hate to generalize, but <b>if you've got an Y chromosome, you're probably not going to like this book because Harper is so adorably girly.</b><br><br><u>THE MOTHEREFFING LOVE TRIANGLE</u>: <blockquote>
  <i>Ryan was a good guy. He always had been.</i>
</blockquote><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397017072ra/9219401.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Harper has a boyfriend, Ryan, and he is absolutely perfect. Handsome, smart, he has supported her throughout her family tragedy. He has stood by her while she joins 1000000 school committees, waiting patiently for her to make time for him. She's been in love with Ryan since 3rd grade, and it took her 6 years to get him. They've been dating for a couple of years, and <b>Ryan is an absolute darling</b>. He is an utter gentleman.<blockquote>
  <i>He lowered his head and kissed me, albeit pretty chastely. PDA is vile, and Ryan, being my Perfect Boyfriend, knows how I feel about it.</i>
</blockquote>He gets along with her friends.<blockquote>
  <i>“Ladies,” Ryan said, nodding at Amanda, Abigail, and Mary Beth. “Let me guess. Y’all are...plotting world domination?”<br>“No,” Amanda told him, deadly serious. “We’re talking about Cotillion.”<br>“Ah, world domination, Cotillion. Same difference,” Ryan replied with an easy grin, and this time, all three girls giggled, even Amanda.</i>
</blockquote>Her parents adore him. He truly is a wonderful guy. He's concerned about her, about all the pressures Harper places on herself.<br><br>And Harper adores him. Until David Stark steps into the picture.<br><br>She and David have known each other since they were children, too, it's a small Southern town, y'all. <b>Harper and David have been each others' nemesis their entire lives, since the cradle, almost.</b><blockquote>
  <i>He and I had loathed each other since kindergarten. Heck, even before that. Mom says he’s the only baby I ever bit in daycare.</i>
</blockquote>It followed through to middle school.<blockquote>
  <i>“I’m sure you’d hate to miss everyone’s <u>felicitations</u>.”<br>David had beaten me in the final round of our sixth-grade spelling bee with that word and now, all these years later, he still tried to drop it into conversation whenever he could.</i>
</blockquote><b>He's taken to writing vicious articles attacking her leadership in school, and implying that she was pregnant.</b> But the instant Harper gets "assigned" to protect him...suddenly, something fucking changes!<blockquote>
  <i>For one horrifying second, I thought he was going to kiss me. I wasn’t really sure how I’d react if he did.<br>But it was only a hug. And if I maybe spent a second or two thinking that he actually smelled really nice, or that he was much more solid than he appeared, so what?</i>
</blockquote>AND SO THE APOCALYPSE BEGINS. Who will it be? Will it be Ryan, lovely boyfriend Ryan who's waiting patiently on the side while Harper gets all her school shit and secret Paladin shit together? Or will it be David?!<blockquote>
  <i>Still, I had to admit, yellow was a good color on him. It brought out the gold in his hair, and—<br>I stopped myself. The gold in his hair? Since when did I care about David.</i>
</blockquote><b>SO WHO WILL SHE MOTHERFUCKING CHOOSE?!</b> Wonderful, neglected Ryan, or asshole-with-a-heart David? And will she ever stop being a motherfucking terrible girlfriend?!<blockquote>
  <i> “But, God, Harper, sometimes I feel like your whole life is a checklist, and I am way down at the bottom. And, you know, every once in awhile, you throw me a bone to keep me happy.”<br>I flinched at that, hard. Not only because it was insulting, but because it was way too close to the truth.</i>
</blockquote><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397017072ra/9219402.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="9346958248400607246" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer796632485" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16753501972239136491"><b>Girls night in!</b><br/>And by that, I mean me, this book and the cat, but shh...<br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395015404i/8935792._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
 <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395015549ra/8935810.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395015549ra/8935811.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><u>This book is pure entertainment.</u> Silly, hilarious fun. I've suddenly realised how hard it is to review a book like this because I cannot lay out the details of some amazingly complex plot... or tell you about the deep philosophical journey you will be taken on... or talk about a rich new fantasy world. This book has none of those things. And yet, it is easily one of the most enjoyable books</span>
  <span id="freeText16753501972239136491" style="display:none"><b>Girls night in!</b><br>And by that, I mean me, this book and the cat, but shh...<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395015404i/8935792._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395015549ra/8935810.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395015549ra/8935811.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>This book is pure entertainment.</u> Silly, hilarious fun. I've suddenly realised how hard it is to review a book like this because I cannot lay out the details of some amazingly complex plot... or tell you about the deep philosophical journey you will be taken on... or talk about a rich new fantasy world. This book has none of those things. And yet, it is easily one of the most enjoyable books I've picked up in a long while.<br><br><i>Rebel Belle</i> is a kind of paranormal, chick-lit comedy thingymabob. I suppose humour is one of the most subjective things, but I'm fairly sure most readers will eat this up like strawberry flavoured ice cream covered in rainbow sprinkles. It reminds me of a young adult, sillier version of the Sookie Stackhouse books (back when they were actually good). But, despite all of that, <b>it really isn't formulaic at all.</b> In fact, this book does quite a lot of new things with the characters, the friendships and the romance, which set it apart from many other YA books and made sure I would have to get my hands on the sequel as soon as possible.<br><br><b>
  <i>I felt like I had stepped into a nightmare. Five minutes ago my main concern had been whether Salmon Fantasy would clash with my pink dress. Now I was cradling a dying man on the bathroom floor while some crazy person pounded on the door.</i>
</b><br><br>Harper Price is the very definition of a Southern belle. She's cheerleading captain, homecoming queen, president of this, that and everything, she has the hottest boyfriend and the most popular friends, and she never EVER says the F-word. That is... until the fateful evening when she finds herself in a strange battle for her life. A battle which ends with Harper acquiring some rather unusual abilities. After that, Harper's perfect little world starts to get very strange indeed. And I 'effin loved it!<br><br>I think Harper is the main reason this book was so good for me. I like characters like her because she wasn't born some gun-toting badass. She's very... <i>girly</i>. Whatever you want to take that to mean. It's possible that some of you won't like her - just as a lot of people didn't like Mac from the Fever series - but I find myself drawn to female characters that are like Harper, you could call them <i>ditzy</i> perhaps, but they show they are able to adapt when the circumstances call for it. They prove that even the blonde cheerleader with the fluffy pom poms can kick ass and save the day. That even the girls who go to parties with their friends, have crushes on boys, trip over their own feet now and then, and have big dreams and ambitions - even they can be superheroes when they find themselves in hot water.<br><br><i>
  <b>“We’re not dead,” he said, almost like he was talking to himself. “How did we not get dead?” <br>I smiled at him and squeezed his arm. “Because I’m awesome.”</b>
</i><br><br>And she is awesome. And hilarious. Both because of the witty things she says and thinks, and also because of some of the embarrassing predicaments she finds herself in. I laughed out loud so many times while reading this book, which is rare.<br><br>It might be light and fluffy but, make no mistake, <i>Rebel Belle</i> is an excellent girl power book. Friendship is extremely important to Harper and there's no casual slut-shaming of the best friend or hidden jealousies lying under the surface. Plus, the main plot line of the book is that Harper is supposed to protect the "Oracle" with her powers and the Oracle is a guy. Interesting and refreshing subversion of gender roles; I'm not going to say too much about their relationship but I really liked how that was handled too.<br><br>In the end, <i>Rebel Belle</i> is mainly a book about a young women who discovers that her life isn't headed down the perfect little path she'd laid out for herself. It's about growing up and adapting to new situations and making the best of what life throws your way. It's a compelling message decorated with pink icing and a lot of laughs. I don't think I can say much more to convince you, so I'll finish with a quote from a funny scene:<br><br><b>
  <i>I picked up the nearest weapon I could lay my hands on: a stapler. I lifted it, going for “menacing.” I admit it lacked a certain elegance, but hey. It was worth a shot. David placed his hand on my arm and pushed it back down.<br>“What?”<br>“Just . . . that’s embarrassing for all of us,” he replied.</i>
</b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="16753501972239136491" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_859236246" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/859236246" />
    <a title="Navessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18104163-navessa"><img alt="Navessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444162983p2/18104163.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/859236246?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Navessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Navessa" href="/user/show/18104163-navessa">Navessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=saved-the-genre">saved-the-genre</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=love-triangle-that-was-not-terribad">love-triangle-that-was-not-terribad</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer859236246" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5146386266419293301"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415028571ra/11718282.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>4.5 STARS</b><br/><br/>Well, that was fucking awesome. Er, sorry. I mean, <i>effing</i> awesome. Not sure the MC of this novel would approve of my swearing in a review. <br/><br/>You see, Harper Price is a southern belle, raised on good manners and tradition. Sure, she might be a little vain, and more than a little self-centered, but that doesn’t necessarily make her a bad person. In fact, she has a sort of self-deprecating sense of humor that makes it pretty hard to hate the girl, regardless of her snobbery. <br/><br/>She reminds me a</span>
  <span id="freeText5146386266419293301" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415028571ra/11718282.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>4.5 STARS</b><br><br>Well, that was fucking awesome. Er, sorry. I mean, <i>effing</i> awesome. Not sure the MC of this novel would approve of my swearing in a review. <br><br>You see, Harper Price is a southern belle, raised on good manners and tradition. Sure, she might be a little vain, and more than a little self-centered, but that doesn’t necessarily make her a bad person. In fact, she has a sort of self-deprecating sense of humor that makes it pretty hard to hate the girl, regardless of her snobbery. <br><br>She reminds me a lot of one of my all-time favorite female leads: Mac, from the <i>Fever</i> series. She’s exactly what I imagine Mac to have been like in high school. She’s your classic over-achiever. Top of her class, head of innumerable school clubs, charity volunteer extraordinaire, you name it. <br><br>Her life is the high school dream your parents tried to get you to believe in. She’s popular, has an incredibly loyal best friend, a dreamy boyfriend, is a shoe-in for prom queen, and will most likely be valedictorian to boot. <br><br>That is until the night of the homecoming dance, when a school janitor locks himself in a bathroom with her and then kisses her before bleeding to death in her arms. As if this isn’t weird enough, immediately afterward, one of her teachers breaks down the bathroom door and tries to kill her. With a scimitar. <br><br>DAFUQ? <br><br>Er, sorry, Harper. <br><br>I mean, DAEFF?<br><br>From that point on her life gets a little crazy. Turns out that janitor was some kind of legendary soldier charged with protecting one of her fellow classmates, and he managed to pass his powers onto Harper through that kiss. <br><br>Oh, and the boy he was charged with protecting, David, happens to be her biggest rival. They’ve competed against each other since they were in diapers. Literally. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“…he and I had loathed each other since kindergarten. Heck, even before that. Mom says he’s the only baby I ever bit in daycare.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Regardless of their animosity, I loved them together. It was obvious from the get-go that these two had chemistry. And passion. And I especially loved that David was anything but your typical, brooding YA “hero”. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“The door swung open, and David stood there, dressed in a yellow sweater and his green corduroy pants. He looked like he should be on PBS, talking to a puppet about the alphabet.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br>*falls over laughing*<br><br>I spent most of this book cackling like a loon and hoping that these two would get over their loathing and realized they were perfect for each other. <br><br>What follows after homecoming is a hilarious tale of the two of them coming to terms with what they both are. This book was filled with fantastic world building, imaginative yet believable lore, and a cast of characters that you can really root for.<br><br>I just…GAH. <br><br>I loved it. I truly did. These kids aren’t idiots. Sure, they’re a little naïve, but they learn from their mistakes, and where a lot of authors would add drama and angst into this storyline (because Harper has a boyfriend that SERIOUSLY factors into the ending of this book), THIS author did not. For which I am eternally thankful. <br><br>This was so good that Hawkins is now on my auto-buy list. <br><br>You should give this book a chance. It might just restore some of your faith in the YA category. <br><br><b><a href="http://www.thealliterates.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thealliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thealliterates" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/the_alliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/thealliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5146386266419293301" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_711333698" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/711333698" />
    <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow"><img alt="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393785730p2/10336538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/711333698?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=the-book-boy-is-mine">the-book-boy-is-mine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=some-kinda-magic">some-kinda-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=favorites-ya">favorites-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=rabid-reads-reviews">rabid-reads-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=southern-comfort">southern-comfort</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer711333698" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer84971072765129314"><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2014/04/review-rebel-belle-by-rachel-hawkins.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/>I was born and raised in the South. My husband was too, but he’s not a <i>real</i> Southerner—his father is from San Francisco, and his mother is from Michigan. They moved to Georgia from up north a few years before the hubs was born, bringin’ their Northern and West Coast ways with them.<br/><br/>Not that there’s anything wrong with Northern or West Coast ways; they just aren’t Southern.<br/><br/>Still aren’t, b/c even after 30+ years of living in the South, there are times when I’ll say or do som</span>
  <span id="freeText84971072765129314" style="display:none"><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2014/04/review-rebel-belle-by-rachel-hawkins.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br /><br />I was born and raised in the South. My husband was too, but he’s not a <i>real</i> Southerner—his father is from San Francisco, and his mother is from Michigan. They moved to Georgia from up north a few years before the hubs was born, bringin’ their Northern and West Coast ways with them.<br /><br />Not that there’s anything wrong with Northern or West Coast ways; they just aren’t Southern.<br /><br />Still aren’t, b/c even after 30+ years of living in the South, there are times when I’ll say or do something, and my husband will be completely bewildered. Or bothered. For example, he particularly dislikes it when I say, “I suwannee.” But I do say it. Regularly. Perhaps even more often than I usually would b/c sometimes it’s fun to bother your husband.<br /><br />*smiles winsomely*<br /><br />The point is that it is a truth universally acknowledged that your family has to have lived in the South for several generations before you are really and truly Southern, and I have a sneaking suspicion that Ms. Hawkins is really and truly Southern, b/c REBEL BELLE captures that essential Southern-ness better than anything I have read in a long, long time.<br /><br />It was positively delightful.<br /><br />I laughed so hard and so often that I was grateful to be reading in the privacy of my own home, AND I read all of it in one sitting. It was that good. Once, I even laughed so hard that I cried. My husband thought I was having a fit. Maybe I was . . .<br /><br />But if I was, I couldn’t help it.<br /><br />With Harper tossing out one-liners left and right, and her crazy great aunts being . . . well, crazy great aunts (and also the source of the longest and loudest laughter), I don’t see how I could possibly be blamed for the perceived hysteria that this book induced.<br /><br />So stop looking at me like I’ve lost my mind, m’kay?<br /><br />And this book has more to offer than just humor. Harper is a character that is easy to connect with whether you’re from the South or not. I’m sure that many of you know someone that deals with grief by making herself too busy to think (or you may even be that kind of person yourself), and that is exactly what Harper is struggling with. She’s the Head Cheerleader, the President of Future Business Leaders of America and the Student Council, Captain of the Debate team, etc.<br /><br />So the last thing she needs is to have superhero-like abilities unceremoniously thrust upon her and the accompanying biological imperative to protect her archnemesis David Stark (a HIPSTER *gasp of horror*).<br /><br />Unfortunately for Harper, that is precisely what happens . . .<br /><br />There weren’t many problems with this book, and the problems I did have weren’t huge. The Big Bad was a little flat; I didn’t understand her or her motivations. She just kind of showed up, this megalomaniac, narcissistic teenager, wrecking havoc wherever she went. And aside from David, who can’t really be considered a secondary, and Harper’s best friend Bee, the other secondaries were also a little bit underdeveloped. Based on the ending, however, I’m hopeful that we’ll learn more about them in the future.<br /><br />But overall REBEL BELLE is sheer perfection for what it is—yummy good brain candy. There are still real problems and obstacles to face, but you don’t become bogged down with trials and tribulations. Harper is a clever girl, capable of thinking on her feet, and if those feet happen to be wearing a pair of fantastic heels—what of it? I highly recommend this book to anyone in need of something lighter and fluffier than the standard Urban Fantasy, YA or otherwise, and I can’t wait to see what the next installment brings.</span>
  <a data-text-id="84971072765129314" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13478373444504151513">This is, quite frankly, the best book I've read this year! (Not including when I reread one of my favourite books :P)<br/><br/>It's funny (I laughed out loud a number of times), it's heartfelt (I felt so bad for our main character quite a few times), it's adorable (so many cute moments between our love interests!), it's aggravating (WHY?!?!), it's surprising (I didn't see a bunch of those plot twists coming!) and it's exciting (WHAT A RIDE!)!<br/><br/>At the heart of a book like this, when you have a heroine who's </span>
  <span id="freeText13478373444504151513" style="display:none">This is, quite frankly, the best book I've read this year! (Not including when I reread one of my favourite books :P)<br /><br />It's funny (I laughed out loud a number of times), it's heartfelt (I felt so bad for our main character quite a few times), it's adorable (so many cute moments between our love interests!), it's aggravating (WHY?!?!), it's surprising (I didn't see a bunch of those plot twists coming!) and it's exciting (WHAT A RIDE!)!<br /><br />At the heart of a book like this, when you have a heroine who's narrating the story from the first person, it's important that you have some type of connection with the lead character, and I so did. I loved Harper! She was bossy and judgemental, but that was okay because she was being Harper and I knew that she wasn't being malicious, she just had a different personality to my own and I appreciated that.<br /><br />Excitingly, I'm going to be doing a full review for this book because while I was reading I kept thinking "I want to talk to my subscribers about this part! And this part! And this part!" So I'm going to! :D<br /><br />Link to review: Coming soon!</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="booksnpenguins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="booksnpenguins" href="/user/show/66222749-booksnpenguins">booksnpenguins</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=ya-na-contemporaries">ya-na-contemporaries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2208157347" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10188190969986124596"><blockquote>
  <i>"When you die in a hundred years, they'll probably write on your gravestone, 'Here Lies Harper Price - Damn It, She Still Had Stuff to Do!”</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><br/>First of all,<br/><a href='https://gifyu.com/image/LG14' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1520199930ra/25162107.gif' alt='ac339c61653d3a21d5455525b176c55c409f30b1fb2a6e425faf22bec8cf2761.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>Second, <br/><a href='https://gifyu.com/image/LG14' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1520199930ra/25162107.gif' alt='ac339c61653d3a21d5455525b176c55c409f30b1fb2a6e425faf22bec8cf2761.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><br/>This book was probably the hugest disappointment I've had since when I was 3 and found out you don't get a candy tree if you plant gummy bears. <br/>I decided to read it because I've been told the main character is both girly and a badass and, in all honesty, I'm soooo done with authors shoving down our throats the same kickass fem</span>
  <span id="freeText10188190969986124596" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"When you die in a hundred years, they'll probably write on your gravestone, 'Here Lies Harper Price - Damn It, She Still Had Stuff to Do!”</i>
</blockquote><br><br><br>First of all,<br><a href="https://gifyu.com/image/LG14" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1520199930ra/25162107.gif" alt="ac339c61653d3a21d5455525b176c55c409f30b1fb2a6e425faf22bec8cf2761.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Second, <br><a href="https://gifyu.com/image/LG14" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1520199930ra/25162107.gif" alt="ac339c61653d3a21d5455525b176c55c409f30b1fb2a6e425faf22bec8cf2761.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>This book was probably the hugest disappointment I've had since when I was 3 and found out you don't get a candy tree if you plant gummy bears. <br>I decided to read it because I've been told the main character is both girly and a badass and, in all honesty, I'm soooo done with authors shoving down our throats the same kickass female characters who despise dresses and everything pink-ish. <br>As if wearing make-up or adoring ballet flats makes you less of a modern woman.<br><br>Anywhoooo...<br>The point is, I've had my reasons to dive into this book feeling like I was about to get some quality girl power action, and instead I found myself with a fistful of cringey moments and the urge to snort some chili pepper in order to feel something.<br><br>Let me be clear. <br>Even if I’m not going to spend any word on the matter, the book itself is not even that bad.<br>The writing is sort of nice and funny in its own frilly way, and I could easily bypass the teenage angst, the plot holes, the cheesy romance and the inaccuracy of the facts.<br>Heck, I could even momentarily forget about how rushed and anticlimactic (and flipping absurd, jesus fries) the ending was…<br>But I could never, ever, ever forgive the author for failing what could have been a pleasant book with one of the worse main characters I’ve read about in the last two years.<br><br>Since it’s only fair to give credit where credit is due, I’ll start this rant by saying that I firmly hate double-standards, and I recognize that Harper has some flaws (things like being so confident and inconsiderate to the point it gets annoying, for example) that could be seen as positive or charming traits if she were a male character. <br>I don’t hate her for these things. <br>I hate her because Harper Jane Price is an uptight, selfish and immature kid who’s the farthest there is from the <i>Badass &amp; Girly</i> hero she’s supposed to represent. <br>I get it, we have to deal with the homecoming queen who comes from a wealthy family, the perfectionist who’s got nothing but straight A+ on her school curriculum, the southern belle who dreams a white wedding with flowers and butterflies, who magically has the chance to turn her life upside down and do <br>I promise, I get it. <br>But still, her nauseating holier-than-thou attitude and inclination to thinking her farts smell like Chanel n. 5, made her almost insufferable to the point I considered dropping the book halfway through it. <br><br>I don’t care if you’re a princess or a peasant, I don’t care if you wear pearls or kombat boots, just don’t be a stupid prick about it. <br>I was so happy to read about a girl who stands out for herself, so happy to relate to someone who shamelessly likes all her girly things and is able to throw powerkicks at the same time, but the case here was different. <br>Harper changed her behavior way too suddenly. <br>She was (almost) cool as long as she was fighing and embracing her destiny as a Paladin, but as soon as boyfriends (plural intended), friends, shoes and school duties were involved, she became the spoiled kid that made me roll my eyes forever (yes, they’re still rolling). <br>I can’t help but think it would have been better to mix these two aspects of her personality together, rather than separating them clearly in two different sides. <br><br>Also, with fact is that, with characters like this one, you’d usually expect a development of some kind, at some point. Our dear Miss Price, on the other hand, has the special ability to become more and more hateful, childish and exasperating as the story goes on.<br><br>Now, I have no idea what southern belle actually are or how they should behave, but according to my beloved Wikipedia, they should be judgy binches who treat people outside of their clique like absolute shit.<br>Exhibit 1: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Harper and her boyfriend of two years, Ryan, conveniently break up literally 2 seconds before the book ends, so (of course) she can go and make out (of course) with her supposed-to-be sort of frenemy, the one she’s being pining over for the entire book (of course) even if she keeps denying her feelings even to poor and broken-hearted Ryan. <br>Nothing too weird about this, if you ask me, but when Ryan becomes the new Mage and joins the happy new couple, she cares so little about him being hurt that she ends up basically throwing her new relationship in his face as if his feelings mean nothing. And to think she has the nerve to say she still love and care about him. At least have the decency to wait a few days???? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>Exhibit 2 (and this was probably the final nail in the coffin):<br><blockquote>”In fact, if I decided to do something so low-class as get a tattoo, […]”</blockquote><br>Well, fuck you, too. <br><br>I mean, it's totally okay if you don't like them, but by saying this is basically like affirming that every single person who has a tattoo is a bag of shit. <br>Ugh, so darn shallow!<br><br>So yeah, lasses and lads. <br>This is what kept this book from gaining more than those two miserable stars. <br>I also feel incredibly frustrated about that cover, because it’s incredibly pretty, but this book doesn’t deserve it. <br>At all.<br><br>As I said before, it makes me a bit sad to give Rebel Belle such low ratings, because the story in general isnt’t even destined for the dump, but I swear I’d rather roll on glowing embers than reading this book once again. <br>Farewell, Rachel Hawkins. <br>May our path cross again.<br>Possibly, under luckier and better bookish circumstances. <br><br><br>Until then, me and my tattoos will be more than happy to avoid <i>Harpy</i>, erm, Harper Jane Price and her inner ugliness like the plague.<br><a href="https://gifyu.com/image/LG14" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1520199930ra/25162107.gif" alt="ac339c61653d3a21d5455525b176c55c409f30b1fb2a6e425faf22bec8cf2761.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Lol</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="10188190969986124596" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2328334198" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2328334198" />
    <a title="Tina Haigler" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30268418-tina-haigler"><img alt="Tina Haigler" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396641790p2/30268418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2328334198?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tina Haigler" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tina Haigler" href="/user/show/30268418-tina-haigler">Tina Haigler</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30268418-tina-haigler?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2328334198" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4859403420141797351"><b>"LOOKING BACK, none of this would have happened if I'd brought lip gloss the night of the Homecoming Dance."</b><br/><br/>Honestly, I didn't know what to expect when I decided to read this. I read it for the pink cover I needed for the color challenge I was doing. I had heard it was funny but worried it was going to be cheesy. Instead it ended up being a lot of fun.<br/><br/>I started out not caring much for Harper, the main character. She came off as a typical sheltered private school rich kid, vapid and self-centered</span>
  <span id="freeText4859403420141797351" style="display:none"><b>"LOOKING BACK, none of this would have happened if I'd brought lip gloss the night of the Homecoming Dance."</b><br /><br />Honestly, I didn't know what to expect when I decided to read this. I read it for the pink cover I needed for the color challenge I was doing. I had heard it was funny but worried it was going to be cheesy. Instead it ended up being a lot of fun.<br /><br />I started out not caring much for Harper, the main character. She came off as a typical sheltered private school rich kid, vapid and self-centered. She had some redeeming qualities though. She was super smart and involved in school activities (even if that was self-serving). She also didn't like to cuss or show PDA, which is rare for a teen. The other main character, David, starts off acting like a tool towards Harper, so I wasn't his biggest fan either. Of course we later find out not all is as it seems, and everything changes. Harper starts caring about people other than herself, and David stops being such a jerk, allowing some emotional attachment to the characters to start building up. There are other characters, a boyfriend, a best friend, and some family members, but none of them seemed to really matter. Saylor was important but the book was in Harper's point of view and they didn't interact with each other much.<br /><br />The plot was definitely interesting. It was cliche in a few places but original in others. I liked how the girl was physically powerful, and in charge of protecting the male character, who was fragile. I also liked how the boyfriend wasn't the center of her life (he was barely in the book), and how sex wasn't the basis of their relationship. They made out a couple of times but it was downplayed and glossed over. I also liked how Harper obeyed her parents, even when she felt they were being unreasonable. Most YA involves teens rebelling but the main character was just trying to be a good kid. After a bit I really started to root for her. I would've liked having more answers but I guess not having them made it a bit more realistic. In real life you tend to figure it out as you go. The mythology was different as well. It introduced a story from history that I was unfamiliar with. The author tweaked it, added some fantasy, and made it her own.<br /><br />I thought this was cute and spunky. I would recommend this to anyone who wants a laid back, fun read. There was violence, but since there's no sex or drugs, or other heavy subjects, and almost no cussing, I consider this suitable for kids as young as 6th grade. My 6th grader is reading it now, and so far she loves it.<br /><br /><b>"And then he placed his palm in mine."</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="4859403420141797351" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1445214640" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1445214640" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1445214640?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780147514356" href="/book/show/22521588-rebel-belle">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Simona by: </span>
      Mila
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=fantastic-lit-and-co">fantastic-lit-and-co</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1445214640" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17083511341911514087">I deem it appropriate to start the year with a good laugh, so: welcome 2016. Let's get started.<br/><br/><b>"I was bringing this by to say sorry for yesterday. To both of you" I added as Saylor moved forward. "You know, for the... the car driving and the recklessness, and the-the grabbing..."<br/>With my free hand I started making this clutching gesture. I was talking about grabbing David's shirt, but it looked like I was milking a cow.<br/>Or worse."</b><br/><br/>This was <i>racy</i>. And yes, I admit it: I laughed like an idiot. Here an</span>
  <span id="freeText17083511341911514087" style="display:none">I deem it appropriate to start the year with a good laugh, so: welcome 2016. Let's get started.<br /><br /><b>"I was bringing this by to say sorry for yesterday. To both of you" I added as Saylor moved forward. "You know, for the... the car driving and the recklessness, and the-the grabbing..."<br />With my free hand I started making this clutching gesture. I was talking about grabbing David's shirt, but it looked like I was milking a cow.<br />Or worse."</b><br /><br />This was <i>racy</i>. And yes, I admit it: I laughed like an idiot. Here and in so many other moments that I lost count of them. And I <i>enjoyed</i> it. I enjoyed a high school drama.<br />It's a new year, guys.<br />In my defense I say there were superpowers. Kind of. Superpowers are always a good excuse. Kind of.<br /><br />•The <b>protagonist</b> of this story, <b>Harper Price</b>, is perfect. Homecoming queen, impossibly high grades, owner of the BBE (Best Boyfriend Ever) aka Ryan Bradshaw. It won't take but a decent amount of nastiness to make her the nightmare and the dream of every teenage girl ever existed. <br />Except she's not.<br />I was sure I was going to have problems with her -beauty queens are not exactly my prototype of favorite main character- but instead I found myself thinking more than once that she is likeable. More than likeable. She's the kind of girl you'd love to have as a friend. She may seem perfect and good at everything she does, and I won't say she is not, but she's not <i>only</i> that: she can get all awkward and ill-at-ease, and if I started to call her names when she almost freaks out for forgetting the lipstick at home, I couldn't help warming to her during the rest of the book. She is <b>competitive, tough, determinate, and she simply doesn't quit</b>. She is the girl, or part of the girl, I'd like to be and try to be.<br /><br />•Of course the<b> plot</b> is not really intricate, and there aren't who-knows-what impredictable plot-twists, but I was expecting none of them. I expected a funny story with easy-going, nice characters, and I got them. Or better, I got more, because this book is also <b>deliciously written</b>. I wasn't prepared to that, but I loved Hawkins' storytelling: being told in first person, Harper also plays as narrator, and she is incredibly good at it. Lovable.<br /><br />➽ Sure, it's not perfect -there are some really silly moments that spoiled my fun a little, but looking to the story as a whole they appear as minor flaws. I am so thrilled about the sequel -I already miss Harper. See? She's like a good friend, I told you.<br />And in case you're wondering, yes, I have a thing for David. What? He's <i>cute</i>. And smart. Smart <i>and</i> cute. Don't try to say you didn't fall for him too, because you don't fool me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17083511341911514087" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12325734999506535310"><u>THIS IS COMING FROM A TRUE SOUTHERN GIRL! PLEASE GO READ REBEL BELLE!</u> <br/><br/>This book is the definition of a GNI (girls night in) book! I wanted a good rom com book to read for a lazy night in..... SO I decided on rebel belle to be my date for the evening, so of course I had to set the mood.... I poured myself a glass of sweet tea, lit some pumpkin candles, and threw on a light blanket and got right into reading it..... and lets just say that <b>Rachel Hawkins didn't disappoint me on this book date.</b> <br/> The</span>
  <span id="freeText12325734999506535310" style="display:none"><u>THIS IS COMING FROM A TRUE SOUTHERN GIRL! PLEASE GO READ REBEL BELLE!</u> <br /><br />This book is the definition of a GNI (girls night in) book! I wanted a good rom com book to read for a lazy night in..... SO I decided on rebel belle to be my date for the evening, so of course I had to set the mood.... I poured myself a glass of sweet tea, lit some pumpkin candles, and threw on a light blanket and got right into reading it..... and lets just say that <b>Rachel Hawkins didn't disappoint me on this book date.</b> <br /> There was an amazing balance between action, comedy, and romance (come on how can you not love a guy wearing a dr. who shirt).<br /><br />I know at this point in time I would normally make some kind of comment about how the book kind of just started... no real build up, background story, or long drawn out family history etc. etc., but I can't. For this story having it just start worked out so well. <br /><br />I loved the way Rachel Hawkins found a kind of comical way of Harper get her powers because its not very often in ya books does a girl get ninja skills from a janitor planting a kiss on her! I loved all the characters, every action scene, and plot twist was perfect!<br /><br />I will not lie though I thought this book looked a little to cheese for me, bc of the cover being head to to pink and pearls, BUT NO IT WAS AWESOME!!! I can't wait to read what I'm hoping will be a trilogy.</span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17702703053833662130">baby's first unpopular opinion!<br/><br/>i read this book a hundred years ago (in 2015), back when i uncritically read everything and enjoyed it, and also i wasn't dead inside, and also i was occasionally pleasant to be around (possibly).<br/><br/>and still i didn't like this book.<br/><br/>i don't remember too much of it, to be honest. the cover does look like i could design it on canva using pinterest-sourced images and that one font everyone uses in their blog headers (this is a call out for me, too. i have not entirely a</span>
  <span id="freeText17702703053833662130" style="display:none">baby's first unpopular opinion!<br /><br />i read this book a hundred years ago (in 2015), back when i uncritically read everything and enjoyed it, and also i wasn't dead inside, and also i was occasionally pleasant to be around (possibly).<br /><br />and still i didn't like this book.<br /><br />i don't remember too much of it, to be honest. the cover does look like i could design it on canva using pinterest-sourced images and that one font everyone uses in their blog headers (this is a call out for me, too. i have not entirely avoided the siren song of tumblr aesthetics). so that's not a point in its favor.<br /><br />overall this is a cool-adjacent idea (even though to be honest, i'm not that into the whole i'm-girly-AND-powerful-wow-give-me-not-like-other-girls-points concept - those 2 things are so obviously not mutually exclusive), which, like every paranormal / urban fantasy book from the early 2010s, grants itself a love triangle and that dumb romance becomes its downfall.<br /><br />if love triangles were any fun to read about, every YA fantasy would still contain them.<br /><br />bottom line: why can't we judge books by their covers again?<br /><br />(this is part of a project i'm doing in which i write reviews of books i read a million years ago, because it's not like i've got anything else going on.)</span>

    <a title="Maggie ☘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40477684-maggie"><img alt="Maggie ☘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591529603p2/40477684.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1206300336?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie ☘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie ☘" href="/user/show/40477684-maggie">Maggie ☘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=great-reads-2016">great-reads-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=amazing-reads">amazing-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=fun">fun</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=charismatic-characters">charismatic-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=witches-magicians">witches-magicians</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=superpowers">superpowers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1206300336" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1924617967730771770"><i>
  <b>“So, Harper Jane Price. Are you ready to accept your destiny?”<br/>I withdrew my hand. “No, thank you.”</b>
</i><br/><br/><br/>On her Homecoming night, soon to be its queen Harper Price experiences very unfortunate encounter in girl's bathroom involving wounded school janitor who kisses Harper before bleeding to death, scimitar wielding history teacher who tries to kill her immediately afterwards and to top of it all Harper experiences a sudden rush of kick-ass powers, which results in Harper killing her teacher with on</span>
  <span id="freeText1924617967730771770" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>“So, Harper Jane Price. Are you ready to accept your destiny?”<br>I withdrew my hand. “No, thank you.”</b>
</i><br><br><br>On her Homecoming night, soon to be its queen Harper Price experiences very unfortunate encounter in girl's bathroom involving wounded school janitor who kisses Harper before bleeding to death, scimitar wielding history teacher who tries to kill her immediately afterwards and to top of it all Harper experiences a sudden rush of kick-ass powers, which results in Harper killing her teacher with one very sharp and very much pink shoe. <br>After that, her lifes turns out to be absolutely effing crazy:<br>1. She's a Palladin.<br>2. David Stark, her lifelong rival and obnoxious school reporter, is the one she should protect.<br>3. Her whole life is going to change.<br><br><br><i>
  <b>"Then I remembered my Professor Giles X could be watching me right now, and probably wouldn’t approve of me slinging rocks at the guy I was clearly supposed to protect.''</b>
</i><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1477353116i/20941301._SY540_.jpg" width="280" height="380" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><i>Rebel Belle</i> was such an <b>entertaining read</b>! The subtle humor and Harper's voice sit absolutely well with me. Her character is like a <b>wonderful mix of Buffy, the Vampire Slayer</b> (from the few episodes I've seen) <b>and Blair Waldorf from Gossip Girl</b>. She's a Southern belle who needs to be always in control of her life, works hard and tries to be perfect in everything in hope of making up for what happened to her sister. <b>Harper loves fashion and dresses, which in no way affect the fact that she's clever, headstrong and very hard working.</b> I liked the fact that she loved fashion but was quite bad-ass, how resourceful and in control she always was, even when lots of people underestimated her for the simple fact that she loved pink, make-up and clothes. I also loved how a certain typical fantasy roles were reversed in this book.<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1477352463i/20941277._SY540_.jpg" width="260" height="290" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>The writing style was swift, to the point and fitting the story. Fast paced plot made it <b>incredibly easy book to read</b>. There is an interesting paranormal aspect involving magic and superpowers, but overall <i>Rebel Belle</i> feels more like a <b>contemporary read mixed with little bit of paranormal elements.</b><br><br><br><i>
  <b>"David’s grin slowly faded and his fingers fiddled with the edge of his T-shirt, pulling it up over his bicep a little. Since when did David Stark have biceps? How did you get any muscle tone when all you did was type and be annoying?”</b>
</i><br><br><br>Aside for the amazing heroine - who is one of the best things about this book - I liked all of the other characters as well.<br> <br><br><i>
  <b>“He and I had loathed each other since kindergarten. Heck, even before that. Mom says he’s the only baby I ever bit in daycare.” </b>
</i><br><br><br>I really enjoyed the kind of <b>hate-to-love relationship</b> Harper and David Stark had going. <br>Harper had a boyfriend beforehand (who was, to my relief, not an asshole to the MC just to make David seem more appealing), but I wouldn't mark this case entirely as a love-triangle. This book was actually surprisingly <b>angst-free</b>. David did suffer a little bit of special-snowflake syndrome, but fortunately, it didn't get obnoxious. <br><b>He reads, has peculiar sense of fashion, loves Lord of the Rings and even through all his sarcasm, is an absolute huggable cutie pie of a human being.</b><br> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1477352694i/20941283._SX540_.png" width="410" height="180" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>This book has also a great family dynamics. No missing parents, which is certainly a bonus! The MC's parents actually have a say in her life. <b>Harper's aunts are awesome trio of old ladies</b>, and I also liked the frienship aspect - her relationship with Bee was another great addition to the story.<br><br><br><b>
  <i>“Go,” she said, giving me a friendly shove. “Get your ninja on.”<br>I reached out to link my pinkie with hers. She squeezed it back. Smiling sheepishly, Bee ducked her head, blond hair swinging over her collarbone. “I forgive you for being a bizarre combination of totally perfect and totally weird.”</i>
</b><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1477353340i/20941319.jpg" width="270" height="380" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>All in all, <b>laugh out loud read</b> with some Gossip Girl elements and some <b>kick-ass superpowers</b>. The heroine is a wonderful Southern belle/overachieving Homecoming queen with love for fashion, great ambitions and newly gotten superhero calling. Rebel Belle is definitely worth getting into when you're tired of heavy books and want something <b>light, uncomplicated, relaxing and entertaining</b>. <br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1477352810i/20941288.jpg" width="270" height="290" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><i>
  <b>“I picked up the nearest weapon I could lay my hands on: a stapler. I lifted it, going for “menacing.” I admit it lacked a certain elegance, but hey. It was worth a shot. David placed his hand on my arm and pushed it back down.<br>“What?”<br>“Just . . . that’s embarrassing for all of us.”</b>
</i><br><br><br>How I (not so surprisingly) imagined Harper:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1477354543i/20941365.jpg" width="250" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="1924617967730771770" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
