  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/921446754" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/921446754?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Teenagers, anyone who wants a great/fun reading.</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Cristina Monica by: </span>
      I saw a lot of my friends reading and enjoying it (myself.)
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=cute">cute</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=loved-it">loved-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=superpowers">superpowers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer921446754" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9565668859930832067">♥ <b>4 ''Loved it!'' stars</b> ♥<br/><br/>This book was so much fun! <b>A breath of fresh air!</b> I actually read this book while eating popcorn. No kidding. If you're looking for something entertaining and purely enjoyable, I highly recommend you <i>Rebel Belle</i>. It also contains a little bit of creepy and/or strange scenes that are only going to make you want to read more and more of it.<br/><br/>Harper might seem to you, at the beggining of the story, a little too girly and vain, but she's actually not that way. She has her reas</span>
  <span id="freeText9565668859930832067" style="display:none">♥ <b>4 ''Loved it!'' stars</b> ♥<br /><br />This book was so much fun! <b>A breath of fresh air!</b> I actually read this book while eating popcorn. No kidding. If you're looking for something entertaining and purely enjoyable, I highly recommend you <i>Rebel Belle</i>. It also contains a little bit of creepy and/or strange scenes that are only going to make you want to read more and more of it.<br /><br />Harper might seem to you, at the beggining of the story, a little too girly and vain, but she's actually not that way. She has her reasons why Homecoming is very important to her that you'll learn eventually in the story. I must admit that her one thousand dollars or more dress made me cringe my teeth. That excepted, Harper is mostly a normal <b>seventeen-year-old</b> teenager dating and loving a nice boy and expecting to pass a great evening at the Homecoming event accompanied by her boyfriend and best friends. Unfortunately, when the school janitor transmits her some weird thing while unexpectingly kissing her, everything changes. And that's when she becomes a <b>kick-ass girl with new superpowers.</b><br /><br />The writing isn't impressive but nice instead. Standard but efficient since a book like this one is better off complicated words and long sentences. It could've been prettier though. This book has a cool atmosphere that'll get you at ease and make the reading comfortable. The story might very likely seem to you either very interesting or fun. Or both. Either way, you'll enjoy it and found it adorable. I thought it was amazing and well done. <b>It felt like watching a comedy/supernatural/drama/action movie.</b> I loved it!<br /><br />The romance was pretty clean. It was cute and sometimes sigh-worthy. And sometimes frustrating indeed. Previsible by moments but also enchanting. Sweet and rightly accompanying the story.<br /><br />If you liked/loved <b>Rachel Hawkins'</b> other books, there are many chances you'll appreciate <i>Rebel Belle</i> too.<br /><br />Happy reading! (And don't forget the popcorn and/or candy!)<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9565668859930832067" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_910079762" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/910079762" />
    <a title="Vanessa J." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19590155-vanessa-j"><img alt="Vanessa J." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468102148p2/19590155.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/910079762?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vanessa J." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vanessa J." href="/user/show/19590155-vanessa-j">Vanessa J.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=overhyped">overhyped</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=lolz-ridiculous">lolz-ridiculous</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=tstl-characters">tstl-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer910079762" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15229582660448070048"><a href='https://bookswithchemistry.wordpress.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433653616i/15127136._SX540_.png' width='350' height='117' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><blockquote>Looking back, none of this would have happened if I’d brought lip gloss the night of the Homecoming Dance.</blockquote><br/><br/>That is the first line of the book. With just that, I already started having bad feels about it. My interest even died with that sinple first line. The ironic thing is... what Harper the perfect Belle says is true: If she hadn't forgotten her goddamned lip-freaking-gloss, there would have been no story.<br/><br/>But really, was there a story? If I remember well, the book started with Harper and he</span>
  <span id="freeText15229582660448070048" style="display:none"><a href="https://bookswithchemistry.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433653616i/15127136._SX540_.png" width="350" height="117" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><blockquote>Looking back, none of this would have happened if I’d brought lip gloss the night of the Homecoming Dance.</blockquote><br><br>That is the first line of the book. With just that, I already started having bad feels about it. My interest even died with that sinple first line. The ironic thing is... what Harper the perfect Belle says is true: If she hadn't forgotten her goddamned lip-freaking-gloss, there would have been no story.<br><br>But really, was there a story? If I remember well, the book started with Harper and her friends at Homecoming party, she forgot her stupid lip gloss, went to the bathroom to put it on, and things started getting weird for fuckery's sake - meaning, everything that happened screamed that the author was trying too hard to make you laugh. All she got from me was:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447201880ra/16969239.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And my expression only varied from that to this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1436564132ra/15478290.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>…in a very short span of time.<br><br>You already know how slim my patience is when it comes to immature or stupid heroines. Since this book was narrated by someone who possessed both traits, it’s no surprise that I ended up despising her. Her way of talking (exactly like Anna from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6936382.Anna_and_the_French_Kiss__Anna_and_the_French_Kiss___1_" title="Anna and the French Kiss (Anna and the French Kiss, #1) by Stephanie Perkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Anna and the French Kiss</a>) was enough of a reason to hate her, but what really put me off was her taboo towards strong words. Let me show you some examples of what she said:<br><br><blockquote>“Oh, this is some bullshit,” I whispered. That’s when I knew I was seriously freaked out. I never curse out loud, not even in private. It’s just not ladylike.</blockquote><br><br><blockquote>She said the actual word. Saylor Stark said the F-word.</blockquote><br><br>There is everything wrong with the first quote. If it contained an ounce of truth, what do you dumb-ass think all women are? Please, even if not all teenagers swear, they’re not scandalized by it, and less even diminish others for doing so. The worst part of that, though, is that she has the stereotyped idea that ladies must not swear because that makes them not-ladies.<br><br>Speaking of stereotypes… Why did all the teenagers here felt formulaic? All the girls obsessed over clothes, make-up, and boys, and all the boys were the typical non-caring. Jesus, not all teenagers are like that! where I studied, it’s true that some people were like that, but it’s never okay to generalize. As a matter of fact, it was a minority the ones who gave more importance to those things than studies.<br><br>Furthermore, the plot (if you consider it a plot) was beyond ridiculous. Let’s say… After what happened with the lip gloss, the janitor came with a sword to Harper, then the History teacher came, she defended herself by killing him and she got superpowers out of the blue. Wtf? What irked me is, as I said, that it tries so hard to be all funny. Harper even jokes about the death of that teacher. Because that’s right: She kills him, and she does not feel shocked, guilty, or pleased or anything about it – she just shrugs it off and jokes about it, and that’s just so unrealistic and enraging.<br><br>Oh, but things get worse. There’s a love triangle, and it takes over the book. And to make it more cliched, it’s between Harper, her boyfriend, and a guy with whom there was mutual hatred. It’s even more annoying because she says things like this:<br><br><blockquote>I had not almost kissed him, I reminded myself. He had almost kissed me, and if he had, I would have pushed him away and made all sorts of shocked sounds, and not kissed him back, even a little bit. I was positive of that.</blockquote><br><br>She sounds as if she’s trying to convince herself there are no feelings, when we, non-idiotic readers, already know she will end up blushing at everything said boy says or does. Much predictable, huh?<br><br>Now, as final words, picture what I said in my pre-review: Your mother baked a delicious cake on Sunday, but not all of it was eaten that day so they put it in the fridge. Some days after, there’s only one slice left, and you remember how delicious the cake was. You go open the door, pick it, and when you’re going to take the first bite you notice there’s mold in it. That feeling you get at that moment – that utter underwhelming sensation and the anger because why didn’t we eat it before? – <i>that</i> is how I feel about this book.<br><br>And Harper, I have some final words for you:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447201880ra/16969240.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>________________________________<br><br><b>Pre-review (November 9th, 2015):</b><br><br>What a goddamn awful book. Do you know how I feel? Picture this: Your mother baked a delicious cake on Sunday, but not all of it was eaten that day so they put it in the fridge. Some days after, there's only one slice left, and you remember how delicious the cake was. You go open the door, pick it, and when you're going to take the first bite you notice there's mold in it. That feeling you get at that moment - that utter underwhelming sensation and the anger because why didn't we eat it before? - <i>that</i> is how I feel about this book.<br><br>More detailed review to come.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15229582660448070048" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1420965594" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1420965594" />
    <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin"><img alt="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603831478p2/17438949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1420965594" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10665029397797189544"><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2015/10/rebel-belle-by-rachel-hawkins.html'>http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.c...</a><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445538712i/16667883.jpg' alt=' : ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Who would have thunk you could be at your homecoming and end up taking someone out with the heel spike of your pink shoe..among other things.</b><br/><br/>All Harper wanted was to get her crown and have a good time with her friends and boyfriend Ryan. But..that wasn't going to happen. Here is a tip, if you forget your lipstick, don't borrow from anyone else and run off to the bathroom to apply... there are weird things that happen in bathrooms. Unless of course you real</span>
  <span id="freeText10665029397797189544" style="display:none"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2015/10/rebel-belle-by-rachel-hawkins.html">http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.c...</a><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445538712i/16667883.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Who would have thunk you could be at your homecoming and end up taking someone out with the heel spike of your pink shoe..among other things.</b><br><br>All Harper wanted was to get her crown and have a good time with her friends and boyfriend Ryan. But..that wasn't going to happen. Here is a tip, if you forget your lipstick, don't borrow from anyone else and run off to the bathroom to apply... there are weird things that happen in bathrooms. Unless of course you really want to become a Paladin and have to protect the boy you loathe the most :) <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445538712i/16667884._SY540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When Harper finally figures out she has become a Paladin and has to protect David Stark, she is not happy. Nope. Nope and Nope. But it's not like you can give it back so onward she goes. <br><br><b>
  <i>At the moment, I really hated that my superpowers prevented me from shaking the crap out of him. I settled for balling my fist up in front of his shirt and pulling him down to meet my eyes. "David, look around you. This? This is crazy-sauce. And if you know anything that could help me figure out why I'm suddenly Wonder Woman, I need to know it right. Effing. Now."</i>
</b><br><br>I can't tell you what they find out that David is.. you will have to read the book. He is something or other and some crazy stuff goes down with all kinds of the kids and some adults in the book. <br><br>I enjoyed the story line and I loved Harper's southern charm..er.. snark! <br><br>I look forward to reading the next book, I didn't even know I would like this book so much, but that's how it goes right? <br><br>They do mention a Hummingbird Cake in the book so I'm going to give you the recipe like a good belle :) Enjoy! <br><br><b>HUMMINGBIRD CAKE</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445538712i/16667885._SX540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Total Time:<br> <br>2 hr 5 min <br><br>Prep: <br>50 min <br><br>Inactive: <br>20 min <br><br>Cook: <br>55 min <br><br>Yield: <br>10 to 12 servings <br><br><u>Ingredients:</u> <br><br>Unsalted butter, for greasing <br>2 3/4 cups all-purpose flour, plus more for dusting <br>1 cup pecan pieces <br>3 ripe bananas, chopped <br>1/2 cup finely chopped fresh pineapple <br>1 teaspoon ground cinnamon <br>1/2 teaspoon freshly grated nutmeg <br>1/2 teaspoon ground ginger <br>1 1/4 teaspoons baking soda <br>1/2 teaspoon salt <br>3 large eggs, at room temperature <br>1 3/4 cups granulated sugar <br>1 cup vegetable oil <br><br><u>For the Frosting:</u> <br>2 packages cream cheese (8 ounces each), at room temperature <br>12 tablespoons unsalted butter, cubed, at room temperature <br>2 cups confectioners' sugar <br>1 tablespoon finely grated lemon zest <br>1 teaspoon vanilla extract<br><br><u>Make the cake:</u> Preheat the oven to 350 degrees F. Butter two 8-inch round cake pans and line with parchment paper. Butter the parchment and dust with flour. <br><br>Spread the pecans on a baking sheet and bake until fragrant and toasted, about 8 minutes. Let cool slightly, then roughly chop. Toss with the bananas, pineapple and 1/2 cup flour in a small bowl. <br><br>Whisk the remaining 2 1/4 cups flour, the cinnamon, nutmeg, ginger, baking soda and salt in a bowl. Beat the eggs and granulated sugar in a separate bowl with a mixer on high speed until thick and light, 5 minutes. Gradually beat in the vegetable oil. <br><br>Sprinkle the flour mixture over the egg mixture, then gently fold to make a thick batter. Fold in the pecan-fruit mixture, then transfer the batter to the prepared pans. Bake until the cakes are firm and a toothpick inserted into the middle comes out clean, 50 to 55 minutes. Cool in the pans on a rack, 25 minutes, then invert the cakes onto the rack to cool completely. <br><br><u>Make the frosting:</u> Beat the cream cheese in a large bowl with a mixer until fluffy, then gradually beat in the butter until combined. Sift the confectioners' sugar over the cream cheese mixture and beat until smooth. Add the lemon zest and vanilla and beat until light and fluffy. <br><br>Place one cake layer on a serving plate. Spread about half of the frosting on top, then cover with the other cake layer. Spread the remaining frosting over the top and sides of the cake. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443579699i/16380381._SX540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>

<div id="review_2317538639" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2317538639" />
    <a title="Nasom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67824881-nasom"><img alt="Nasom" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520213174p2/67824881.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2317538639?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nasom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nasom" href="/user/show/67824881-nasom">Nasom</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67824881-nasom?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2317538639" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10826206177936894361"><b> Rating: 4.5 </b><br/><br/><b> Full Review </b><br/>This book is like legally blonde but instead of the main character, Harper, realizing she’s smart, she realizes she’s got superpowers.<br/><br/><b> Plot </b>: 17-year-old Harper Price was in school for homecoming, where she was to be crowned queen. She goes to the bathroom to apply some lip gloss (I think) and as she’s in the bathroom, the school’s janitor comes in and before you know it, he passed his powers to her. Apparently, he was something called “Paladin” which Harper is now. Now</span>
  <span id="freeText10826206177936894361" style="display:none"><b> Rating: 4.5 </b><br /><br /><b> Full Review </b><br />This book is like legally blonde but instead of the main character, Harper, realizing she’s smart, she realizes she’s got superpowers.<br /><br /><b> Plot </b>: 17-year-old Harper Price was in school for homecoming, where she was to be crowned queen. She goes to the bathroom to apply some lip gloss (I think) and as she’s in the bathroom, the school’s janitor comes in and before you know it, he passed his powers to her. Apparently, he was something called “Paladin” which Harper is now. Now Harper finds that she has all this power and what’s worse? She now has to protect the boy she’s hated since she was little. <br /><br /><b>Thoughts! </b><br />- I found the plot interesting and unique. I don’t think I’ve read many books with a male damsel in distress (a woman being the protector of a guy who has zero fighting skills). I think the only other one I can think of is Vin/Elend from the Mistborn Series. So it was cool seeing the girl being the sole protector<br />- I also enjoyed the southern belle-turned-superhero plot. Harper goes from worrying about dresses, school functions and the perfect boyfriend to worrying about protecting her archenemies from being killed.<br />- I loved the comedy aspect of it. I laughed quite a lot of times, especially during Harper’s inner monologues. She reminded me of all the girls in the high school shows/movies I loved <br />- There was a love triangle which made me weary but I respected how it was handled. I expected a “Current-boyfriend-turns-A-hole-to-make-way-for-new-love-interest” situation but it was not like that at all and I really appreciate that.<br />- Harper doesn’t like people swearing/cursing which I related to bc same lol <br /><br />If you’re looking for a fun, no-stress read, I recommend this. <br /><br /><b> Initial Thoughts </b><br />This was such a fun easy read and I laughed so much. Who knew a book about a southern belle with superpowers could be this enjoyable? <br /><br />RTC</span>
  <a data-text-id="10826206177936894361" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_898839492" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/898839492" />
    <a title="Kassidy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8937622-kassidy"><img alt="Kassidy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585073850p2/8937622.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/898839492?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kassidy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kassidy" href="/user/show/8937622-kassidy">Kassidy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8937622-kassidy?shelf=2014-release">2014-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8937622-kassidy?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8937622-kassidy?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer898839492" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16352392337784457119">*4.5*<br/><br/>I adored this book~<br/><br/>It's a cute, funny, realistic book that packs a huge punch! <br/>This book almost reads like contemporary, but has an underlying fantasy plot. <br/>I really loved the characters. The main character Harper is a southern girl, who is very dedicated to her school, studies, friends, boyfriend, and community. If that isn't enough to handle, she is thrown into the position of the Paladin and discovers a whole magical world she never knew existed. <br/> I really loved reading about Harper and </span>
  <span id="freeText16352392337784457119" style="display:none">*4.5*<br /><br />I adored this book~<br /><br />It's a cute, funny, realistic book that packs a huge punch! <br />This book almost reads like contemporary, but has an underlying fantasy plot. <br />I really loved the characters. The main character Harper is a southern girl, who is very dedicated to her school, studies, friends, boyfriend, and community. If that isn't enough to handle, she is thrown into the position of the Paladin and discovers a whole magical world she never knew existed. <br /> I really loved reading about Harper and it was very interesting seeing her try to deal with this new life. The other characters were great as well, no one was who they seemed to be. My first impressions of the characters weren't that great, I thought Harper was a little bitchy, and David (who is Harper's arch nemesis, but becomes a critical person in her life) was a jerk and annoying. However, I was surprised at how much I enjoyed getting to know them all, and at who they turned out to be! <br />There is a bit of romance and I have to say at points I was a little aggravated with it. Although, in the end, I love how it turned out and I was pleasantly surprised by the development of the romance and characters.<br />I think one of the best things about this book is how realistic it is, I felt like the characters dealt and reacted to everything in a feasible way. The complexities of the situation were really explored.<br />The pacing was also great, I liked that the fantastical elements were introduced and explained early on. Throughout the story there are questions and answers and everything is building up to a crazy ending.<br />The writing is super easy to read and I thought some of the jokes were so so funny! <br />I would say that much of the book is predictable, but there were definitely some curve balls.<br />Overall, it's a slower story with a lot of character and plot development, but an easy, fun read!<br />I don't think it is a book for everyone. However, if you like a witty and determined main character, who does have some faults, but ultimately goes through a lot of growth, as well as some romance drama, along with a little weird and crazy, then I think this might be a book for you!<br /><br />Thank you to Penguin Publishing for sending me a copy of this book in return for an honest review!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16352392337784457119" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Harper Price, our protagonist, is the town’s golden girl: Southern belle, Homecoming Queen, SGA president, and 4.0 GPA student. But what this golden girl doesn’t know is that her life is going to take a drastic detour (and all because she forgot her lipgloss.   <span id="freeText9573187211601425086" style="display:none"><br />Well. . . after having so many of my lovely goodreads friends encouraging me to read this book, I have finally given into peer pressure!<br /><br /><i> Rebel Belle </i> is quite an unusual book. Harper Price, our protagonist, is the town’s golden girl: Southern belle, Homecoming Queen, SGA president, and 4.0 GPA student. But what this golden girl doesn’t know is that her life is going to take a drastic detour (and all because she forgot her lipgloss. Ugh, don’t you just <i> hate </i> when that happens?)<br /><br />I don’t want you to be fooled by my rating. I actually quite enjoyed this book. It was hilarious (this girl can kick some serious butt and still manage to look fabulous). Harper is such a fun main character. Her commentary and censoring of swear words (me too, girl, me too) is literally the best thing ever. <br /><br />So the plot was interesting and actually quite unique. I was intrigued while I read the story but I still felt like <i> something </i> was missing (I’m not quite sure what is it, so don’t ask me - still trying to figure it out myself). <br /><br />I enjoyed the banter between the characters, it was easy, realistic, and hella entertaining to read. <br /><br />The plot twist was like ‘whoa, didn’t see that one coming’ and I’m not entirely sure if it’s going to make the series more interesting or more forced. Idk, I guess that is yet to be seen. <br /><br />I’m hoping the next books will continue along with the hilarity and original-ish plot (I’ve heard a lot of reviews saying that the coming books are kinda a downgrade in comparison AND I’m <i> really </i> hoping that’s not the case.)<br /><br /><i> “It's always going to get better someday. Sometime in the future, things won't be so crazy.” </i><br /><br />3.5 stars!!</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_140288115" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/140288115" />
    <a title="Kylee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3688270-kylee"><img alt="Kylee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579467814p2/3688270.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/140288115?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kylee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kylee" href="/user/show/3688270-kylee">Kylee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer140288115" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14329580806235145626">You might not know this about me, but I’m actually not a huge girly girl. I don’t really like pink, I don’t wear makeup, I wouldn’t dream of casually wearing heels, and I think beauty pageants are just ridiculous. Instead, I usually rock jeans and a nerdy t-shirt, spend my time reading fantasy books or gaming with my guy friends, and I swear worse than my brother. So just looking at this cover had me a little hesitant, and when I read the summary, I was ready to chuck this book in the fire. But,</span>
  <span id="freeText14329580806235145626" style="display:none">You might not know this about me, but I’m actually not a huge girly girl. I don’t really like pink, I don’t wear makeup, I wouldn’t dream of casually wearing heels, and I think beauty pageants are just ridiculous. Instead, I usually rock jeans and a nerdy t-shirt, spend my time reading fantasy books or gaming with my guy friends, and I swear worse than my brother. So just looking at this cover had me a little hesitant, and when I read the summary, I was ready to chuck this book in the fire. But, through the sheer power of will and the overwhelming fear of being murdered by my reader friends if I didn’t finish this book, I started the first page. And didn’t put the book down once. Yeah, you heard me. I busted this book in a few hours, finishing at about one in the morning, very alarmed to see it was that late because I hadn’t even noticed the time passing. I liked this book. I liked this book with its pink cover and perky heroine and silly dresses and lighthearted magic stuff. It was actually kind of… cute.<br /><br />In Rebel Belle, we meet Harper, the sort of girl that I probably would have avoided in high school. She’s head of practically every club or leadership related thing in the school, she says cutesy little things instead of swearing, she spent over a thousand dollars on her Homecoming dress and she keeps her lips perfectly glossed at all times. Right off, I did not like Harper one bit. But as the pages flew by, she started to grow on me. Under that perfect, perky exterior, Harper had a tough, loyal, fun side to her that I adored. She ends up getting super Paladin powers from her janitor, and suddenly she can kick ass. Like, really kick ass. Like, she stabbed someone in the throat with her heel. Suddenly, girly shoes became a lot more interesting to me. She was fierce and strong and confident, and I love how self-sufficient she was. This girl doesn’t need anyone, and I loved it. Harper actually had more layers than I expected, an unending arsenal of witty comebacks, and a whole lot of spunk.<br /><br />Then we meet David, the boy that Harper is supposed to protect with her new-found powers. Because he may or may not be very very special. The only problem is, they absolutely despise each other. I mean, they hate each other with a fiery passion. David is the hipster guy that wears corduroy pants and writes stories for the school newspaper, occasionally pointing out bad things about Harper, which is unacceptable. But when they are forced to work together, she realizes that David might not be so bad after all. I adored David. Let’s just say that it takes a special kind of guy to deal with Harper. And he is such a cutie, I almost couldn’t handle it. Did I mention that he likes Doctor Who and Lord of the Rings and probably a plethora of other adorable nerdy things? Cue the wistful sighing. Anyways, David has some secrets of his own, but most importantly, under those layers of v-necks and striped sweaters, he has a big heart of gold.<br /><br />One of the only problems I had with this book was the big fat love-triangle that was determined to drag itself out through the whole book. Harper, of course, starts to deal with some questionable feelings about David, all while she is dating the most perfect boyfriend possible, Ryan. And Ryan is a good guy and a pretty awesome boyfriend, I’ll give him that. The things is, as far as love triangles go, this is probably the type that I find to be the most acceptable. Where the girl has a steady boyfriend then meets the new guy and starts to like him. That’s an okay thing to happen and a lot less annoying than two guys suddenly taking an interest in a girl and fighting to the death over her. No thanks. The problem in this book though was that it just went on and on. And I get that Harper has this weird thing with having to be the best and keeping things perfect, so possibly not liking her perfect boyfriend is scary and all, but she should have dropped him from like page one. Watching her run back and forth between the two of them got frustrating after like the first ten times it happened.<br /><br />As far as the plot goes, it was really cutesy and fun. Rachel Hawkins really has a way of making her books just an enjoyable, lighthearted read while still making you care about the characters and I love it. Since I adored the characters and their interactions, it made the book a million times better. The only problem was that not a whole lot really happens. The beginning took right off with Harper getting her powers and killing a guy, then finding out what all she could do and a few things including a car chase. I mean, it was a great start and it really draws you in. But then, things start to slow down. Now I obviously loved this book and raced through it, but once I was done, there was kind of that moment where I looked back and realized not a whole lot actually happened. Most of the book is just character interaction and trying to solve a few mysteries and a few bad guys trying to do bad stuff, but not a whole lot besides that.<br /><br />Also, the whole Paladin, while original, was a little lacking. I enjoyed it just because it was a new thing I’d never read about, but there just wasn’t really anything about it to make it unique or memorable. Basically, Harper being a Paladin just meant that she has super fighting skills now and a strong urge to protect David from harm. So while I did like the magic elements in this book, everything seemed kind of mashed together with no clear connection. We are given some back-story to the whole Paladin thing, but it wasn’t really strong mythology and seemed a little discombobulated. But by the end of this book, it feels like there are still lots of things that Harper and David don’t know yet, so maybe we will get more explanations in the next book, and hopefully, it can bring the mythology together a bit better.<br /><br />The thing about this book though is that despite the few things that I didn’t like, I still had a great time reading this book. I was giggling and cheering and covering my eyes at the embarrassing parts. I loved Harper and David and their friends and the little Southern town they live in and all the people in it. This book is definitely a cutesy book, but it still won me over purely because it is so cute and fun. Honestly, if you have any girly bone in your body, something about this book will probably appeal to you, as long as you can deal with the few technical issues.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14329580806235145626" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1397772826" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1397772826" />
    <a title="Jilly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly"><img alt="Jilly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435955932p2/25894509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1397772826?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jilly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jilly" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly">Jilly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=y-a">y-a</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1397772826" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16061157071514395314">The author described this book as a cross between "Legally Blonde" and "The Terminator", and that is a good description. I would have used "Legally Blonde" and "Buffy, the Vampire Slayer" myself, though. This is a seriously fun book!<br/><br/>Our hero is Harper, a proper southern belle. She is an over-achiever and completely in love with herself. At first, she is a little annoying, but once you get to know her better, you end up loving her. It just has that funny, quirky feel when there is this girl in pi</span>
  <span id="freeText16061157071514395314" style="display:none">The author described this book as a cross between "Legally Blonde" and "The Terminator", and that is a good description. I would have used "Legally Blonde" and "Buffy, the Vampire Slayer" myself, though. This is a seriously fun book!<br><br>Our hero is Harper, a proper southern belle. She is an over-achiever and completely in love with herself. At first, she is a little annoying, but once you get to know her better, you end up loving her. It just has that funny, quirky feel when there is this girl in pink suddenly becoming this magical Paladin (a guardian for Oracles).<br><br>Harper has a nemesis: David Stark. He and Harper have hated each other since grade-school and do everything they can to upset the other one. David is a total hipster, and Harper hates the way he dresses:<br><br><b>
  <i>David stood there, dressed in a yellow sweater and his green corduroy pants. He looked like he should be on PBS, talking to a puppet about the alphabet.</i>
</b><br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/sesame%20street" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1443055250ra/16311416.gif" alt="sesame street photo: *Dancing on Sesame street* a11fea09.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The problem is that when Harper realizes she is a Paladin that is supposed to guard someone with her life, she finds out that David is the person she is supposed to guard. Not cool!!<br><br>David is the first male oracle in a century, and unfortunately for him, that means there are a lot of people who want to kill him. And, according to his vision, shit's gonna go down at Harper's cotillion. Yes, cotillion. It's a southern thing...<br><br>So, Harper is trying to juggle all of her over-crowded schedule with a boyfriend, <i>and</i> do this Paladin thing. It doesn't go well....<br><br>All together, this story, and the characters, is really cute and funny. I loved Harper and David, and all of the quirky characters in between - like Harper's very old, very adorable aunts. I would suggest this book to anyone who is looking for a light and fun read, and liked Buffy. I would especially recommend it to anyone who lives in the south because it hits the nail on the head in that regard!<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="16061157071514395314" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Hadya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55852574-hadya"><img alt="Hadya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586011465p2/55852574.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2046654912?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hadya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hadya" href="/user/show/55852574-hadya">Hadya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2046654912" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1856104631579383676"><b> 3.75 stars </b> <br/><br/><br/><blockquote> <i> <b> I had just killed a teacher. <br/>With my shoe </b> </i> </blockquote> <br/><br/>I can practically feel myself slowly crawling out of a hole labelled "slump"<br/>After 7 days of not being able to finish a single book I started, I stumbled across Rebel Belle, well more like every where I looked everyone was reading this and I tried to ignore it until I couldn't anymore, and finally, I finshed a book.<br/><br/>This book is about a homecoming-queen turned spiderman, getting all those cool assassin powers, and having to protect a guy</span>
  <span id="freeText1856104631579383676" style="display:none"><b> 3.75 stars </b> <br /><br /><br /><blockquote> <i> <b> I had just killed a teacher. <br />With my shoe </b> </i> </blockquote> <br /><br />I can practically feel myself slowly crawling out of a hole labelled "slump"<br />After 7 days of not being able to finish a single book I started, I stumbled across Rebel Belle, well more like every where I looked everyone was reading this and I tried to ignore it until I couldn't anymore, and finally, I finshed a book.<br /><br />This book is about a homecoming-queen turned spiderman, getting all those cool assassin powers, and having to protect a guy she hates.<br />That's about as non spoilery a summary you can get.<br /><br />This book was awesome tbh, I mean she kills a guy with a pink sparkly shoe (not a spoiler, literally happens on like the 8th page), why wouldn't I want go read about that.<br /><br />The ship in this book was the cutest thing ever, if you know me, you know I love hate-to-love relationships, and David and Harper were precisely that, if you didn't get that from the non spoilery summary. Plus it was a slow burn romance, I cant count the number of times I squealed lol.<br /><br /><br /><br />But I guess this was a light read?? because there were many things I tried to settle with, knowing it was a light read and light reads don't go in depth on topics, but I really couldn't just not think of it. <br /><br /><br /><b> Minor spoilers from here, major are marked </b><br /><br /> <br />Firstly, she kills a guy, next day is perfectly fine, no one just goes from "stab stab" to "fixing their makeup" Like I get it, she had a few nauseous moments, but even in self defense, <u> she killed him </u> and she saw <u> a person die </u> but she focused more on her "superhero powers" and forgot all about it. I mean its not every day that a seventeen year old homecoming queen kills her history teacher, so I would've just liked it if it was given just a tiny bit more attention tbh.<br /><br />In the end of the book <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ when Saylor dies and Bee gets taken, David didn't take a few weeks off to mourn for his Aunt, admittedly she wasn't his real aunt, but he's know her since he was a baby, he didn't even cry I think. And Harper didn't rampage when her best friend got taken, but instead the next day after Cotillion, Harper and David started dating?????  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />So yeah I don't think Light reads are mainly my thing but this was a good book though.<br /><br />So um read it? okay bye.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1856104631579383676" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/ddU/tEGGIPeswy70F/aLSnWaMClH7SVe3L6+9xPZO4gWiI1IzxD8vHIHUhxjtbJj8vBfTV1Hj7kpiT/yKMxYQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NTFlHJV8SNpTZX6KH6f0Ws2nOb9Q2k2NBTFrcRznBLLovBPXZ0YTq3web3m+dvi+a7qQAsCw5yaa5bV1CAtRPQ==')})
  }
